  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2828006d-14bb-4996-8b54-ffaa36596b56'

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer826042452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2087555678479859468">I was worried that I would be missing huge plot lines beginning with book #3 the Rise of Mallory but I was wrong. Everville 3: The Rise of Mallory reads like a separate novel with small references to the past but nothing that prevents the reader from fully grasping the storyline.<br/><br/>I enjoyed this book immensely. It is action packed with well developed characters who were easy to love or hate equally. Each character is clearly defined. I was quickly absorbed in the plot rooting for Owen, Zee and Ani</span>
  <span id="freeText2087555678479859468" style="display:none">I was worried that I would be missing huge plot lines beginning with book #3 the Rise of Mallory but I was wrong. Everville 3: The Rise of Mallory reads like a separate novel with small references to the past but nothing that prevents the reader from fully grasping the storyline.<br /><br />I enjoyed this book immensely. It is action packed with well developed characters who were easy to love or hate equally. Each character is clearly defined. I was quickly absorbed in the plot rooting for Owen, Zee and Anika while quietly hissing at Mallory. There are many layers to this book and I have just purchased Books 1 and 2 so that I can fully appreciate the story and to better get to know these deep and wonderful characters. The scenery is is explained in wonderful detail and I loved the duo worlds.<br /><br />It ended much to soon for this first time reader but happily I can now go back to the beginning and get my fill while I anxiously await the next instalment. <br /><br />This book is ideal for all fantasy lovers and will not disappoint. Bravo Roy Huff.<br /><br />I was provided with a draft in order to perform an honest review. All opinions are my own.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer804895323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16794542213866830033">Roy Huff does it again, in a well developed action packed adventure that appeals to the same part of me that loves thrill rides, Halloween, and classic horror movies.<br/>I always like to read a series in order, but this has enough background that it could certainly be read alone.<br/>Descriptions are vivid and the plot well executed in The rise of Mallory. <br/>With alternate realities and monsters, I must confess that they are always the biggest attraction for me.<br/>The cover for this book is amazing, and the s</span>
  <span id="freeText16794542213866830033" style="display:none">Roy Huff does it again, in a well developed action packed adventure that appeals to the same part of me that loves thrill rides, Halloween, and classic horror movies.<br />I always like to read a series in order, but this has enough background that it could certainly be read alone.<br />Descriptions are vivid and the plot well executed in The rise of Mallory. <br />With alternate realities and monsters, I must confess that they are always the biggest attraction for me.<br />The cover for this book is amazing, and the story does not disappoint, highlighting the values of friendship, trust and honour.<br />The characters develop further, growing up nicely in the this book. The open ending was a good decision, as I can already see how the series could go even further.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer797017479" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4474440117995764169">This is certainly the best book in the series so far. It is action-packed, we get to know a little more about the other realms and new race, the Alarians, which I really enjoyed, they are very unique. The final battle was very thrilling!<br/>The character development in this book is also nicely done, Owen Sage and his friends feel like real persons with their own personalities and problems. <br/>Once again the ending came too soon, so I can't wait to find out what's next for Owen, Zee, Anika and others!<br/><br/>Th</span>
  <span id="freeText4474440117995764169" style="display:none">This is certainly the best book in the series so far. It is action-packed, we get to know a little more about the other realms and new race, the Alarians, which I really enjoyed, they are very unique. The final battle was very thrilling!<br />The character development in this book is also nicely done, Owen Sage and his friends feel like real persons with their own personalities and problems. <br />Once again the ending came too soon, so I can't wait to find out what's next for Owen, Zee, Anika and others!<br /><br />Thanks again to Roy Huff for sending me a draft!</span>

<div id="review_803780424" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/803780424" />
    <a title="Anne-Rae Vasquez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12926930-anne-rae-vasquez"><img alt="Anne-Rae Vasquez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442643607p2/12926930.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/803780424?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne-Rae Vasquez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne-Rae Vasquez" href="/user/show/12926930-anne-rae-vasquez">Anne-Rae Vasquez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12926930-anne-rae-vasquez?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer803780424" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3503232793606823950">In The Rise of Mallory, the newest book in the Everville series, the epic journey continues with another battle to save Everville and Earth. Truths are revealed about Owen and his friends while more interesting creatures are introduced and the lines between good and evil are blurred. The battle escalates into a breathless climax leaving just enough for readers to anticipate more for future books in the series.<br/><br/>What I enjoyed is Huff's ability to seamlessly tie in the earthly world and then throw </span>
  <span id="freeText3503232793606823950" style="display:none">In The Rise of Mallory, the newest book in the Everville series, the epic journey continues with another battle to save Everville and Earth. Truths are revealed about Owen and his friends while more interesting creatures are introduced and the lines between good and evil are blurred. The battle escalates into a breathless climax leaving just enough for readers to anticipate more for future books in the series.<br /><br />What I enjoyed is Huff's ability to seamlessly tie in the earthly world and then throw the reader into the fantasy world where mystical and magical creatures live. When I was reading the Everville series, it reminded me vaguely of A Wrinkle in Time by Madeleine L'Engle with young adventurers on a crusade to an unknown magical place.<br /><br />Young readers, or anyone who likes fantasy adventures, will be entertained with this exciting series. Many questions from the previous books will be answered and fans of the Everville series will be pleased with the third installment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3503232793606823950" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer717747351" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12330983115831287768">I was given an ARC by the author and asked for an honest review.<br/><br/>The Rise of Mallory is the third installment of the Everville series (following The First Pillar and The City of Worms). Again, the author has delivered a well-written adventure that makes you want to keep reading and not put the book down. Our hero, Owen Sage, is asked to do something unbelievable to stop an evil plot to take over and destroy Everville residents as well as other species in our and other universes. A well-written pl</span>
  <span id="freeText12330983115831287768" style="display:none">I was given an ARC by the author and asked for an honest review.<br /><br />The Rise of Mallory is the third installment of the Everville series (following The First Pillar and The City of Worms). Again, the author has delivered a well-written adventure that makes you want to keep reading and not put the book down. Our hero, Owen Sage, is asked to do something unbelievable to stop an evil plot to take over and destroy Everville residents as well as other species in our and other universes. A well-written plot, lots of action and twists, great characters (some even disappear), portals and even a dragon! That's all I'm saying, don't want to spoil it for anyone.<br /><br />If you haven't read any of the Everville books but you enjoy sci-fi/alternate universe stories, then you really have to read these books. You won't be disappointed!<br /><br />I want to thank the author, Roy Huff, for letting me read for him, these books are great reads. Can't wait for the next Owen Sage adventure!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12330983115831287768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/716451101" />

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/716451101?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Siina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Siina" href="/user/show/8755528-siina">Siina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18713493-the-rise-of-mallory">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8755528-siina?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8755528-siina?shelf=beta-review">beta-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8755528-siina?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8755528-siina?shelf=fantasy-scifi">fantasy-scifi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer716451101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer735950175471342638">I got this book for a beta purpose as I got the former parts too. The Rise of Mallory was surely the strongest of the three books. Huff finally depicts his characters and the worlds with detail making them vivid thus bringing them to life. The human characters act more like adults, which is great, since they are that basically already. Overall we get to know the characters better, which is always great. The plot works out nicely too and the open ending was a good choice. I'd say the book is thre</span>
  <span id="freeText735950175471342638" style="display:none">I got this book for a beta purpose as I got the former parts too. The Rise of Mallory was surely the strongest of the three books. Huff finally depicts his characters and the worlds with detail making them vivid thus bringing them to life. The human characters act more like adults, which is great, since they are that basically already. Overall we get to know the characters better, which is always great. The plot works out nicely too and the open ending was a good choice. I'd say the book is three stars though way more steadier than the other parts. I'm happy to see that Huff has developed as a writer in such a short time, so points for that!<br /><br />About the problems then. The war takes a bit too much of the book and there are problems with the time line. After some time the war doesn't really offer us anything new and becomes mundane. The depictions of the sides leans towards the other side on the other side's cost. Moving back and forth in time is always a challenge too, since one must remember where the character stands in order to make the time work towards the right direction. Along these, we have the human characters. Huff forgets them (except Owen of course) after he gets the war mode going, and that sadly so makes the book lacking. What went on in the human world when all these things happened in Everville?<br /><br />Even with its "flaws" the book is entertaining and good continuation to the series. So, congratulations Roy! </span>
  <a data-text-id="735950175471342638" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11151058079594782886"> Everville 3: The Rise of Mallory by Roy Huff is the third book in the Everville series. It picks up right where book 2 left off with Owen and his friends on Earth preparing for Christmas. The cast in Everville is trying to return to their normal lives as they recover from adventures of the last book as well.<br/><br/>Mallory is now raising a surprisingly powerful dragon that he intends to use for the forces of Them in their fight against The Keepers.   <span id="freeText11151058079594782886" style="display:none"> Everville 3: The Rise of Mallory by Roy Huff is the third book in the Everville series. It picks up right where book 2 left off with Owen and his friends on Earth preparing for Christmas. The cast in Everville is trying to return to their normal lives as they recover from adventures of the last book as well.<br /><br />Mallory is now raising a surprisingly powerful dragon that he intends to use for the forces of Them in their fight against The Keepers. Owen and his Everville allies know that they must prepare for a coming attack even when they are unsure of how or when it will come. Everyone must do what they can to prepare for the upcoming fight.<br /><br />And it isn’t only the good who are preparing, Mallory and his minions understand that their attack would come most effectively from a new, unexpected direction. If The Keepers are almost the most powerful force in the universe, where can Mallory find someone he hopes is even stronger?<br /><br />Such a gathering of strength might be avoided, but this can only be done with a great personal sacrifice. Just how much will Owen be willing to endure so that he might have a chance to save everything? For how very long? He might find that his original goal becomes abstract when it’s pitted against new, unforeseen happiness.</span>

<div id="review_836792568" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/836792568" />
    <a title="Anna Tan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6091742-anna-tan"><img alt="Anna Tan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442643502p2/6091742.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/836792568?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna Tan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna Tan" href="/user/show/6091742-anna-tan">Anna Tan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18713493-the-rise-of-mallory">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6091742-anna-tan?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer836792568" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3008454804824050984">Since the last battle in Everville, Mallory, a Fron turned evil, plots to hoard all the power from the element for himself by harnessing the goodwill of the newly hatched dragon, Rathlar, and initiating an inter-universe war between the Alarians and the inhabitants Everville. Owen faces his toughest task yet and struggles to complete it even whilst his friends are being decimated by the Alarians. <br/><br/>I think The Rise of Mallory was better written than the first two (maybe because of experience?). A </span>
  <span id="freeText3008454804824050984" style="display:none">Since the last battle in Everville, Mallory, a Fron turned evil, plots to hoard all the power from the element for himself by harnessing the goodwill of the newly hatched dragon, Rathlar, and initiating an inter-universe war between the Alarians and the inhabitants Everville. Owen faces his toughest task yet and struggles to complete it even whilst his friends are being decimated by the Alarians. <br /><br />I think The Rise of Mallory was better written than the first two (maybe because of experience?). A few typos noted - I think he'll probably fix this? Anyway, this could be an early copy since I borrowed it on Kindle Prime (free trial! ha!).<br /><br />The story is more complex and Huff manages to weave most of the seemingly loose ends from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17404695.The_First_Pillar__Everville___1_" title="The First Pillar (Everville, #1) by Roy Huff" rel="nofollow noopener">The First Pillar</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17968674.The_City_of_Worms__Everville___2_" title="The City of Worms (Everville, #2) by Roy Huff" rel="nofollow noopener">The City of Worms</a>. However, in usual form, Huff messes up the narrative through excessive info dumps, taking you back and forth over the material a few times. I don't know why he can't do a slow reveal of some of these "secrets" through conversations or over several chapters rather than telling you "this and that" happened in one chapter and then a chapter later someone confirms "yes, it really happened".<br /><br />There's some time jumps back and forth due to the nature of Owen's task too - and while it was interesting (life as an Alarian!) I felt that it was a little under-developed. I mean, he could have done SO MUCH MORE with it. <br /><br />At any rate, I think this rates about a 2.5 stars. Hopefully the next one gets better. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3008454804824050984" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Anna (Enchanted by YA)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya"><img alt="Anna (Enchanted by YA)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426518362p2/30983445.jpg" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer10281161258877688558"><i>***I received the eBook free as a review copy from the author in exchange for an honest review***</i><br/><br/>The Rise of Mallory is easily the best book in the series so far, and in my eyes a fitting end to all the character’s story. I understand that there is still 1 (at least) book(s) to be written and published but I love the way that this book was concluded and while it’s unusual for me to stop a series half way through to me it has been concluded in the most satisfying way. Even with minor plotlines st</span>
  <span id="freeText10281161258877688558" style="display:none"><i>***I received the eBook free as a review copy from the author in exchange for an honest review***</i><br /><br />The Rise of Mallory is easily the best book in the series so far, and in my eyes a fitting end to all the character’s story. I understand that there is still 1 (at least) book(s) to be written and published but I love the way that this book was concluded and while it’s unusual for me to stop a series half way through to me it has been concluded in the most satisfying way. Even with minor plotlines still left open.<br /><br />It wasn’t just the ending that made this the best book, but I finally felt true connections to the characters which was something I’d not realised how much I’d missed. This then helped the pace as well as increasing my interest. There was a also lot less time spent on scheming and more on the results of the plans. Of course there was still a lot, especially with Mallory who played a much bigger part than before.<br /><br />With him comes disaster for Owen as he faces yet another life-changing decision. To choose between his original goal for which he sacrificed so much, and remembering the beautiful shreds of happiness he found in such a low time; his decision won’t be easy.<br /><br />They never have been, in this captivating series.<br /><br />Posted on: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">http://enchantedbyya.blogspot.co.uk/</a></span>

<div id="review_829129480" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/829129480" />
    <a title="Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5782335-nicole"><img alt="Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556226587p2/5782335.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/829129480?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole" href="/user/show/5782335-nicole">Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5782335-nicole?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5782335-nicole?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5782335-nicole?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5782335-nicole?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer829129480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12920167897978694842">I had a hard time connecting with this title in the Everville series. For one thing, while some reviewers have said that this could be a stand-alone work, I have to disagree. It's been a while since I read the previous books, and I was seriously lost for a good portion of this installment. There were a lot of characters I had difficulty placing, and there are a lot of references to previous plot points that you really are going to need to have fresh in your memory. That made the initial chapters</span>
  <span id="freeText12920167897978694842" style="display:none">I had a hard time connecting with this title in the Everville series. For one thing, while some reviewers have said that this could be a stand-alone work, I have to disagree. It's been a while since I read the previous books, and I was seriously lost for a good portion of this installment. There were a lot of characters I had difficulty placing, and there are a lot of references to previous plot points that you really are going to need to have fresh in your memory. That made the initial chapters a bit frustrating.<br /><br />There isn't much character development and the majority of characters felt flat to me. Which is really problematic since there aren't many new characters. Add really stilted dialogue, and the problems start to compound.<br /><br />Finally, there is a lot of exposition and repetition - particularly in regard to the battle and the events that lead up to it. Please don't spend an entire chapter on a world-building history lesson just to have a character repeat that entire history three chapters later.<br /><br />I have to admit I skimmed a lot of the last third of this book. I wish I could recommend this series, but it still needs a lot of work.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12920167897978694842" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6301369051553927919">Everville 3: The Rise of Mallory by Roy Huff is an excellent YA fantasy that will keep you on the edge of your seat. It is fast paced, action packed adventure that is hard to put down once you start reading.<br/><br/>The author is a great storyteller, able to bring the story to life. It is easy to put yourself into the tale and follow along as an unseen character. The story is realistic and full of exciting twist and turns in the plot, yet easy to follow along.<br/><br/>This is book 3 of Roy Huff Everville series a</span>
  <span id="freeText6301369051553927919" style="display:none">Everville 3: The Rise of Mallory by Roy Huff is an excellent YA fantasy that will keep you on the edge of your seat. It is fast paced, action packed adventure that is hard to put down once you start reading.<br /><br />The author is a great storyteller, able to bring the story to life. It is easy to put yourself into the tale and follow along as an unseen character. The story is realistic and full of exciting twist and turns in the plot, yet easy to follow along.<br /><br />This is book 3 of Roy Huff Everville series and the author continues to build and strengthen the characters and especially the hero. I found it very easy to identify with them and found myself cheering them on. <br /><br />I really like The Rise of Mallory by Roy Huff and I highly recommend this book to all readers.<br /><br /><br />[Please note: I was given a free copy of this book in exchange for my honest review.]<br /></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2537188785" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2537188785?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sheila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sheila" href="/user/show/2039269-sheila">Sheila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2039269-sheila?shelf=scifi-fantasy">scifi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2039269-sheila?shelf=teen-fiction">teen-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2537188785" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16809571983104459265">With references back to characters and events of the previous books, Everville the Rise of Mallory is a fitting conclusion to the storyline begun in The First Pillar. The stories are best read in sequence though, and the story continues with the Fall of Brackenbone and, hopefully, more to come.<br/><br/>Complex world (and multiverse) building, with fascinating alien species, epic battles, great good and great evil characterize these novels, together with wise understanding of human nature. Arrogance is a </span>
  <span id="freeText16809571983104459265" style="display:none">With references back to characters and events of the previous books, Everville the Rise of Mallory is a fitting conclusion to the storyline begun in The First Pillar. The stories are best read in sequence though, and the story continues with the Fall of Brackenbone and, hopefully, more to come.<br /><br />Complex world (and multiverse) building, with fascinating alien species, epic battles, great good and great evil characterize these novels, together with wise understanding of human nature. Arrogance is a weakness and patience a truly surprising strength, especially when applied to time-travel. Meanwhile rules set up behind the scenes keep everything in order, even when the evil Mallory begins his own re-creation so very coolly described.<br /><br />The lessons learned in this tale are wise. The story’s exciting. And the resolution, though a little hurried, is genuinely satisfying. There’s lots of potential for more stories and “myths” in this series, and I would certainly read them.<br /><br />Disclosure: I bought it on a deal and I enjoyed it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16809571983104459265" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer880028206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2571061066640473147">Definitely my favorite book of the series. <br/>I just couldn't put this book down. <br/>There is a lot happening in Everville and on Earth and Owen is going to take you through a long journey to understand the Third Pillar of Truth.<br/>All the little things bugging me in the previous books of the series have disappeared, making this book my absolute favorite.<br/>I love how we don't dig into the characters all that much, but are instead allowed to follow them as they try to understand what is happing. I also like</span>
  <span id="freeText2571061066640473147" style="display:none">Definitely my favorite book of the series. <br />I just couldn't put this book down. <br />There is a lot happening in Everville and on Earth and Owen is going to take you through a long journey to understand the Third Pillar of Truth.<br />All the little things bugging me in the previous books of the series have disappeared, making this book my absolute favorite.<br />I love how we don't dig into the characters all that much, but are instead allowed to follow them as they try to understand what is happing. I also like how Owen is growing more confident and more able to do things on his own instead of relying too much on people back on Earth. <br />The fact that there is a lot going on in so many different places made this book a delight of complexity, but was at the same time easy to read which is a proof of the author's hard work as that sort of narrative is very difficult to efficiently put off.<br />The test the Third Pillar gave to Owen was also a very good one. I know I complained about the previous one but this one was really incredible and unexpected. And the reward for it was also on that order of magnitude which made me very happy.<br /><br />Seriously, I can't wait to read book four. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2571061066640473147" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1260171117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14911672515216817370">As always Roy Huff has done an excellent job with this third story in his series. In this third book we find Owen Sage, the hero trying to protect both his world and teh world of Everville from Mallory. If he fails it could mean the destruction of people, animals and other creatures in both worlds. He is not alone in this effort. He has the help of Zee and Anika. Like his other books this book is fast paced filled with twists and turns. His world building as always is great. He seems to be able </span>
  <span id="freeText14911672515216817370" style="display:none">As always Roy Huff has done an excellent job with this third story in his series. In this third book we find Owen Sage, the hero trying to protect both his world and teh world of Everville from Mallory. If he fails it could mean the destruction of people, animals and other creatures in both worlds. He is not alone in this effort. He has the help of Zee and Anika. Like his other books this book is fast paced filled with twists and turns. His world building as always is great. He seems to be able to create our world and the world of Everville so they flow together. If you haven't read this series yet I would suggest you begin it. His next book will be out very soon.</span>

<div id="review_1347511618" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1347511618" />
    <a title="M.M. Strawberry Library &amp; Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12558730-m-m-strawberry-library-reviews"><img alt="M.M. Strawberry Library &amp; Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346883958p2/12558730.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1347511618?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="M.M. Strawberry Library &amp; Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="M.M. Strawberry Library &amp; Reviews" href="/user/show/12558730-m-m-strawberry-library-reviews">M.M. Strawberry Library &amp; Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1347511618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7885105545781076996">After having read the first two books, I was eager to read this next one. We are introduced to a new race, the Alarians, and we learn more about the element and its creation/purpose.<br/><br/>I feel that the author did a bit more telling than showing in some parts, as some parts felt a bit rushed through and it was hard for me to visualize what was going on, but I still very much enjoyed this book, and read the fourth book right after this. If you read and enjoyed books 1 and 2, then continue the series a</span>
  <span id="freeText7885105545781076996" style="display:none">After having read the first two books, I was eager to read this next one. We are introduced to a new race, the Alarians, and we learn more about the element and its creation/purpose.<br /><br />I feel that the author did a bit more telling than showing in some parts, as some parts felt a bit rushed through and it was hard for me to visualize what was going on, but I still very much enjoyed this book, and read the fourth book right after this. If you read and enjoyed books 1 and 2, then continue the series and pick up this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7885105545781076996" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1377367154775642408">A scintillating read!<br/><br/><br/>Epic fantasy is not this reviewer’s preferred genre. But that’s where the negatives end! This is a scintillating read. Fast-paced, thrilling, entertaining. It held me to the end.<br/><br/>It’s a tale with many levels – and very well written. Easy to see why it’s the Readers' Favorite 2014 Young Adult Fantasy Silver Medal Winner!<br/><br/>Great cover, too. They say, never judge a book by its cover…. Well, this one breaks the rule.<br/></span>

<div id="review_876047395" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/876047395" />
    <a title="Kim Lo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12149505-kim-lo"><img alt="Kim Lo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458659649p2/12149505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/876047395?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim Lo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim Lo" href="/user/show/12149505-kim-lo">Kim Lo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18713493-the-rise-of-mallory">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer876047395" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3052134748206791982">Continuing on the journey of Owen in Everville, he is met with a surprise when he realizes that someone close to him appears to him to reveal to him the dangers that arose from the results of the City of Worms. Owen is faced with Mallory, a Fron turned evil who has a thirst for collecting power from the element. Owen is now sent off to look for the Third Pillar by the Keeper in hopes of finding a way to stop the war which is claiming innocent lives as the war continues. <br/><br/>Definitely one of most co</span>
  <span id="freeText3052134748206791982" style="display:none">Continuing on the journey of Owen in Everville, he is met with a surprise when he realizes that someone close to him appears to him to reveal to him the dangers that arose from the results of the City of Worms. Owen is faced with Mallory, a Fron turned evil who has a thirst for collecting power from the element. Owen is now sent off to look for the Third Pillar by the Keeper in hopes of finding a way to stop the war which is claiming innocent lives as the war continues. <br /><br />Definitely one of most complete of the Everville series so far, Owen has a better character development. There is more action and mystery surrounding what is going on. I'm still getting used to the writing style however, it does illustrate what is going on with all the characters. The plot thickens and its becoming a more fluent and intriguing read than the previous times. <br /><br />Whats great is that its not as confusing as the first, and not dragged out as the second. This one maintains a fast pace and keeps multiple parts going on simultaneously without being too hard to follow. There was a few times, I had to go back to gather the situation but it was a very rare occasion. <br /><br />A fantastic follow-up to the previous book and the best installment in the Everville series so far!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3052134748206791982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1286420696" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1286420696" />
    <a title="Jane Blanchard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7332241-jane-blanchard"><img alt="Jane Blanchard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442634505p2/7332241.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1286420696?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane Blanchard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane Blanchard" href="/user/show/7332241-jane-blanchard">Jane Blanchard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1286420696" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8426073708584126893">Everville: The Rise of Mallory by Roy Huff is the third book in the Everville fantasy series written for young adults. There is a lot of backfill, but I recommend reading the books in order to fully understand the epic struggle.<br/><br/>In this book, Owen Sage visits the third Pillar of Truth to learn how to combat Mallory and his dragon, Rathlar. Meanwhile, the other worlds are preparing for a war that could end of the multiverse, their world as the know it.<br/><br/>As an adult, I did not find this book as engag</span>
  <span id="freeText8426073708584126893" style="display:none">Everville: The Rise of Mallory by Roy Huff is the third book in the Everville fantasy series written for young adults. There is a lot of backfill, but I recommend reading the books in order to fully understand the epic struggle.<br /><br />In this book, Owen Sage visits the third Pillar of Truth to learn how to combat Mallory and his dragon, Rathlar. Meanwhile, the other worlds are preparing for a war that could end of the multiverse, their world as the know it.<br /><br />As an adult, I did not find this book as engaging as the first two books: the characters were flat and not as well-developed, the dialog did not flow as well, the plot seemed too convenient, and there were quite a few typos and grammar errors.<br /><br />On the other hand, Mr. Huff's description of the shape-shifting Alarians is very imaginative as is Owen Sage's method of saving the world, though his conversation with Rathlar was not very convincing,<br /><br />There are still mysteries in Everville and 4 Pillars of Truth for Owen Sage to visit. I hope Mr. Huff can take his time with the next installment and delivery a story that is a satisfying as the first two books in this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8426073708584126893" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/NS4Er22liRnDnIExnpO9taBjdGMGWI4JorLSHXXASEnbUudZPRjp7g5KTUpBX2A/9XWMg0U69iWWUY63S9D4A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jG2w1WMA3cRYmJIZ37hzCb9QEEzEOfobOPWkWBdJo4xX1ENaukIoR4evySgwx0B/lgRLr0U0c/uIJikqv7HhTQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Oblomov\'s distinguishing characteristic is his slothful attitude towards life. While a common negative characteristic, Oblomov raises this trait to an art form, conducting his little daily business apathetically from his bed. \n\nWhile clearly comedic, the novel also seriously examines many critical issues that faced Russian society in the nineteenth century. Some of these problems included the uselessness of landowners and gentry in a feudal society that did not encourage innovation or reform, the complex relations between members of different classes of   <span id="freeText8554352769693364733" style="display:none">Roy Huff is a Hawaii-based best-selling author, peer-reviewed research scientist, and teacher. After overcoming significant childhood poverty in the US mainland, he moved to the islands and hasn't looked back.<br /><br />Despite his challenges, which include a family stricken by mental illness and the loss of a father to HIV/AIDS, he’s earned five degrees, trained on geostationary satellites for NASA's GOES-R Proving Ground, and has written numerous bestsellers.<br /><br />Roy embraces optimism, science, and creativity and hopes you’ll come along for the amazing ride.
